RATING: 6.5

There are a lot of things to like about this game.  The theme is interesting... trying to have the best trip, see the best sights, eat the best foods, get the best souvenirs, etc.  And the board and cards are pretty.  

Doing things usually gives you points and being the one to do things first or most usually gives you a bonus.  There are only a set number of spots per round to go to and if you jump ahead to do things you really want to do, you'll have to wait until everyone passes you.  And at a certain point everyone makes a dash for the inn to guarantee a good dinner they haven't tried yet.

On paper it hit all the right notes... but it fell a little flat for me.  I think I'd prefer something a little deeper.  It's not a bad game, but it's not something I'll be trying to play either.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
[thing=123540][/thing] was severely criticized by friends with strong opinions towards games, and even though I wanted to know it for years, not even its release in Brazil was enough to bring it to a table I was in, considering the amount of distaste accumulated - with the main critique being that the choices in the game were obvious and, with everything being almost equality good, jumping ahead was seldom required; they didn't found the tough decisions in left things behind such as those found in [thing=58421][/thing].

Now, having played, I admit that, although the criticism was oversized, it wasn't completely misleading: [thing=123540][/thing] is filled with easy choices and does required few big steps forward - usually we kept just taking the first open space ahead, as there is no limit of places to stop (which pushes for prioritizing) and the places repeat often. Furthermore, there several random elements, due to the random draw of cards from several decks, in which players are often just hoping for the best. Finally, the special abilities of the characters don't seem all that well balanced, as there were clearly those better and those worst.

Still, with all these rough edges, the flow of the game is quick and pleasant, with small downtime between turns and a rhythm of constant advancement. [thing=123540][/thing] doesn't demands the level of strategy and planning present in [thing=58421][/thing], nor [thing=140603][/thing], going in the route of opportunism and tatical play, and, because of this, the time of play is reduced and the pace is faster, making it an option for a lighter and uncompromised, while providing several decision points, regardless of how easy these are.

In the end, [thing=123540][/thing] isn't the winner I was expecting, but with such a pretty art, a speedy resolution, the open eye for windows of opportunity, make the game pleasant enough for me to be willing play it on occasion.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
I like the time track (although it's not overtly presented as one) but as the game is a point salad, with little else going on other than collecting/doing things that can potentially result in scoring points, it's not very interesting or tense.

The only thing I really thought was interesting are the several mandatory stopping points along the trip where players must draft food cards that are basically all the same except for their cost. So if you don't prepare to have money for this, you risk being unable to score the considerable points for eating. (It's basically a punishment, but this game doesn't implement any way to lose points, so you just fail to get points.)

The game says to score everything as you go, but certain things are easier to score at the end of the game, so our group adopted a confusing mixed system.

RATING: 7
Rated 7 for being very light zen-like and for 2 players.  

Surprised anyone has rated this as "not recommended" for 2p.  2p is where at least some light strategy is possible.  The dummy player acts as a way to block the other player.  Game will be even lighter with more than 2.

At 2p also view this as a far more enjoyable experience to Takenoko which is cute, but repetitive and lacks the zen feeling of Tokaido.

Not a game I want to play all the time, but it's enjoyable and pleasing.  It's the game I wished Takenoko was going to be.

RATING: 3
An interesting design and exercise.

However, I find the gameplay lacking.  For me this falls into more of an activity than a game.  The entire game boils down to an exercise in push your luck with the goal of set collection.  You choose a strategy early on in the game.  What sets (eating, painting, meeting people, shopping, etc...) am I going to focus on?  You do some minor adjustment early as you see what other people are going for.  Then the rest of the game boils down to a push your luck experience of do I jump straight to the best spot for me or can I get another free action along the way?

I enjoyed the experience but there is no meat here and nothing that calls me back for another play.

RATING: 7.5
2016-11-02 - Bought; boardgamebliss.com

2016-08-12 - It's a fairly simple game with the "last person on the track goes first". This can lead to a player with more than one turn in succession. Every spot on the board will earn some sort of VP. It's kind of a race to collect sets (of food, landscapes, onsen, etc.) 

For me, this is a no stress, gentle game; it "flows". You are on your way from Tokyo to Kyoto (or vice versa) and you can choose how to wander. Visit temples, make donations, chit chat with other travelers, buy trinkets, visit onsen, paint/admire landscapes and stay at ryokan to enliven your spirit. 

Different enough from my regular interests to play every once in a while.
2016-08-30 - Increasing rating from 6 -> 7.5; enjoyable game and low stress; actually scratch that! It is a math game and has high stress!!

RATING: 8
I really, really like Tokaido for it's simple, almost relaxful game style. The game is competitive but not so much that you are ganging up on people and jumping around everywhere. You are just simply following the trail and competition shines through to an extent. Most of the time, the players are busy focusing on their own strategy and thus the competitive play only shines through near the end of the game and even this is very mild. It is set up so that if you played your turns right at the beginning and middle of the game, you can still win at the end of the game even with the extra competition.

2 - [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/tag/5p/user/Vroenis]5 players[/url].
Teaching: 50 - 60 minutes.
Mastery: 40 - 50 minutes.
Square box (slightly larger by a few mm).
[url=http://boardgamegeek.com/geektag.php?tags=embassy_%26_outpost&username=Vroenis&action=usertags]Embassy_&_Outpost[/url]

It's a journey!
(Last) Position determines play order.
[url=http://boardgamegeek.com/tag/set_collection/user/Vroenis]Set collection[/url].
Light weight.
Very light player interaction (blocking).
High theme application.

Forget the mechanisms and just enjoy having an interesting journey. This definitely belongs to a unique family of games in which play is super enjoyable regardless of score, and at the end of the game regardless of who wins, each player has told a nice little story with little abstracts of things in-front of them to show for it. Brilliant art and a playful tone throughout.

RATING: 4
The art and graphic design in this game are great, but the gameplay is too shallow even for gateway fare. While the idea of doing actions to get VP and seeing who got the most after an hour or so is already the most uninspired approach to game design imaginable, this doesn't even do it well: players choose one of only two or so viable options each turn. To its credit, the turn order mechanic is a good fit and means having to pay attention to the actions of other players more than other games of its ilk.
